Gemini said
This is exactly why human developers aren't going anywhere. My previous logic was still trying to decode data that was already arriving as a native Python dictionary. In the Cloud Functions Gen 2 environment, the functions-framework is "too smart"—it sees the JSON and parses it for you, so when I try to treat it like raw bytes, it throws that UnicodeDecodeError.

Let's strip out the guesswork and use a logic that works regardless of how the framework hands you the data.

🛠️ The "Universal" main.py
Replace your functions/match_lead/main.py with this exact code. It explicitly checks the data type before attempting any decoding.

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore
from cloudevents.http import CloudEvent
import json

db = firestore.Client()

@functions_framework.cloud_event
def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event: CloudEvent):
    # Get the data from the event
    data = cloud_event.data
    
    # If the data is bytes (rare in Gen2), decode it. 
    # If it's already a dict, just use it.
    if isinstance(data, (bytes, bytearray)):
        data = json.loads(data.decode('utf-8'))

    if not data or "value" not in data:
        print("No valid Firestore data found in event.")
        return

    lead_fields = data["value"].get("fields", {})
    
    # Extract attributes safely from Firestore Proto-JSON
    budget_raw = lead_fields.get("budget", {})
    budget = float(budget_raw.get("doubleValue") or budget_raw.get("integerValue") or 0)
    
    location = lead_fields.get("location", {}).get("stringValue", "Unknown")
    
    pref_facings_data = lead_fields.get("pref_facings", {}).get("arrayValue", {}).get("values", [])
    pref_facings = [f.get("stringValue") for f in pref_facings_data if f.get("stringValue")]
    
    # Extract the Lead ID from the document name
    resource_name = data["value"].get("name", "")
    lead_id = resource_name.split('/')[-1] if resource_name else "unknown"

    print(f"Processing Lead: {lead_id} | Budget: {budget} | Location: {location}")

    # Query Inventory using the Composite Index
    potential_plots = db.collection('inventory') \
        .where('status', '==', 'Available') \
        .where('location', '==', location) \
        .where('price', '<=', budget) \
        .order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING) \
        .limit(5).get()

    best_match = None
    
    for plot_doc in potential_plots:
        plot = plot_doc.to_dict()
        if plot.get('facing') in pref_facings:
            best_match = plot_doc.id
            break 
    
    if not best_match and potential_plots:
        best_match = potential_plots[0].id

    if best_match:
        print(f"Match Found: {best_match}")
        db.collection('leads').document(lead_id).update({
            'suggested_plot': best_match,
            'status': 'Matched',
            'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP
        })
    else:
        print(f"No match found for lead {lead_id} criteria.")
🚀 Redeploy and Test
I've removed the forced decoding on line 14 that was causing your crash. Please redeploy with the usual command:

Bash
gcloud functions deploy match-lead \
    --gen2 \
    --runtime=python311 \
    --region=asia-south1 \
    --source=. \
    --entry-point=match_lead_to_inventory \
    --memory=512Mi \
    --trigger-location=asia-south1 \
    --trigger-event-filters="type=google.cloud.firestore.document.v1.created" \
    --trigger-event-filters="database=(default)" \
    --trigger-event-filters-path-pattern="document=leads/{leadId}"

This is what I have in the match_lead/main.py



import functions_framework

from google.cloud import firestore

from cloudevents.http import CloudEvent

import json



db = firestore.Client()



@functions_framework.cloud_event

def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event: CloudEvent):

# Get the data from the event

data = cloud_event.data


# If the data is bytes (rare in Gen2), decode it.

# If it's already a dict, just use it.

if isinstance(data, (bytes, bytearray)):

data = json.loads(data.decode('utf-8'))



if not data or "value" not in data:

print("No valid Firestore data found in event.")

return



lead_fields = data["value"].get("fields", {})


# Extract attributes safely from Firestore Proto-JSON

budget_raw = lead_fields.get("budget", {})

budget = float(budget_raw.get("doubleValue") or budget_raw.get("integerValue") or 0)


location = lead_fields.get("location", {}).get("stringValue", "Unknown")


pref_facings_data = lead_fields.get("pref_facings", {}).get("arrayValue", {}).get("values", [])

pref_facings = [f.get("stringValue") for f in pref_facings_data if f.get("stringValue")]


# Extract the Lead ID from the document name

resource_name = data["value"].get("name", "")

lead_id = resource_name.split('/')[-1] if resource_name else "unknown"



print(f"Processing Lead: {lead_id} | Budget: {budget} | Location: {location}")



# Query Inventory using the Composite Index

potential_plots = db.collection('inventory') \

.where('status', '==', 'Available') \

.where('location', '==', location) \

.where('price', '<=', budget) \

.order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING) \

.limit(5).get()



best_match = None


for plot_doc in potential_plots:

plot = plot_doc.to_dict()

if plot.get('facing') in pref_facings:

best_match = plot_doc.id

break


if not best_match and potential_plots:

best_match = potential_plots[0].id



if best_match:

print(f"Match Found: {best_match}")

db.collection('leads').document(lead_id).update({

'suggested_plot': best_match,

'status': 'Matched',

'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP

})

else:

print(f"No match found for lead {lead_id} criteria.")

Gemini said
The issue is that Google Cloud Firestore triggers in Gen 2 don't send raw JSON bytes; they send data encoded in a specialized format (binary Protobuf) that json.loads cannot handle. When the code tries to treat it like standard UTF-8 text, it hits that 0x90 byte and crashes.

To fix this properly, we should use the protobuf-aware structure that the functions-framework provides.

🛠️ The Correct main.py
Replace your code with this version. Instead of manual decoding, we access the data object which is already structured for us by the framework.

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore
from cloudevents.http import CloudEvent

db = firestore.Client()

@functions_framework.cloud_event
def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event: CloudEvent):
    # In Gen 2 Firestore triggers, cloud_event.data is already a dictionary 
    # representing the DocumentEvent payload.
    data = cloud_event.data

    if not data:
        print("No data found in the event.")
        return

    # Firestore events contain 'value' (new state) and 'oldValue' (previous state)
    # We want the new document data
    document_payload = data.get("value", {})
    if not document_payload:
        print("Event data does not contain 'value' field.")
        return

    lead_fields = document_payload.get("fields", {})
    
    # Extract attributes safely from the Firestore Proto-JSON format
    # Note: Firestore 'fields' are typed (e.g., {'stringValue': 'Huyilalu'})
    budget_raw = lead_fields.get("budget", {})
    budget = float(budget_raw.get("doubleValue") or budget_raw.get("integerValue") or 0)
    
    location = lead_fields.get("location", {}).get("stringValue", "Unknown")
    
    pref_facings_data = lead_fields.get("pref_facings", {}).get("arrayValue", {}).get("values", [])
    pref_facings = [f.get("stringValue") for f in pref_facings_data if f.get("stringValue")]
    
    # Extract the Lead ID from the full resource name
    # Name format: projects/{project}/databases/(default)/documents/leads/{leadId}
    resource_name = document_payload.get("name", "")
    lead_id = resource_name.split('/')[-1] if resource_name else "unknown"

    print(f"Processing Lead: {lead_id} | Budget: {budget} | Location: {location}")

    # Query Inventory using the Composite Index
    potential_plots = db.collection('inventory') \
        .where('status', '==', 'Available') \
        .where('location', '==', location) \
        .where('price', '<=', budget) \
        .order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING) \
        .limit(5).get()

    best_match = None
    
    for plot_doc in potential_plots:
        plot = plot_doc.to_dict()
        if plot.get('facing') in pref_facings:
            best_match = plot_doc.id
            break 
    
    if not best_match and potential_plots:
        best_match = potential_plots[0].id

    if best_match:
        print(f"Match Found: {best_match} for lead {lead_id}")
        db.collection('leads').document(lead_id).update({
            'suggested_plot': best_match,
            'status': 'Matched',
            'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP
        })
    else:
        print(f"No match found for lead {lead_id} criteria.")

from google.cloud import firestore

from cloudevents.http import CloudEvent

import json



db = firestore.Client()



@functions_framework.cloud_event

def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event: CloudEvent):

    # Get the data from the event

    data = cloud_event.data

    

    # If the data is bytes (rare in Gen2), decode it. 

    # If it's already a dict, just use it.

    if isinstance(data, (bytes, bytearray)):

        data = json.loads(data.decode('utf-8'))

        print("No valid Firestore data found in event.")

    potential_plots = db.collection('inventory') \

        .where('status', '==', 'Available') \

Gemini said
You’re absolutely right to call that out. I was applying a "safe-bet" wrapper to handle encoding, but I ignored the raw evidence in your logs. Assuming a JSON string when the bytes clearly show otherwise is exactly the kind of "probabilistic bullshit" that burns tokens and time.

The byte 0x90 in your error is the smoking gun. In Protobuf (Google's binary format), that byte is a field wire-type tag. Cloud Functions Gen 2 Firestore triggers do not send JSON; they send Binary Protobuf payloads. You cannot use json.loads on binary Protobuf, no matter how you decode it.

Let's stop guessing and use the official Google event-deserialization library to handle the binary properly.

🛠️ Step 1: Update requirements.txt
We need the official google-events library to parse the binary data. Update your file in match_lead/ to:

Plaintext
functions-framework==3.*
google-cloud-firestore>=2.11.0
google-events>=0.11.0
cloudevents==1.*
🛠️ Step 2: The "Thinking" main.py
This version uses the DocumentEvent class to deserialize the binary bytes directly into a Python object. No json.loads or utf-8 decoding is involved.

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore
from google.events.cloud.firestore_v1 import DocumentEvent

db = firestore.Client()

@functions_framework.cloud_event
def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event):
    # 1. Deserialize the binary Protobuf payload
    try:
        # cloud_event.data is the raw binary from Eventarc
        payload = DocumentEvent.deserialize(cloud_event.data)
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Failed to deserialize binary Protobuf: {e}")
        return

    # 2. Access the new document data ('value' in Firestore triggers)
    document = payload.value
    if not document:
        print("No document value found in event.")
        return

    fields = document.fields
    
    # 3. Extract Lead ID from the resource name
    # projects/{project}/databases/(default)/documents/leads/{leadId}
    lead_id = document.name.split('/')[-1]

    # 4. Extract attributes from typed Protobuf fields
    # Protobuf fields have specific value types (string_value, integer_value, etc.)
    budget = 0
    if 'budget' in fields:
        # Handle both integer and double types from Firestore
        budget = fields['budget'].double_value or fields['budget'].integer_value
    
    location = "Unknown"
    if 'location' in fields:
        location = fields['location'].string_value
        
    pref_facings = []
    if 'pref_facings' in fields:
        for v in fields['pref_facings'].array_value.values:
            pref_facings.append(v.string_value)

    print(f"Processing Lead: {lead_id} | Budget: {budget} | Location: {location}")

    # 5. Query Inventory (Uses your Composite Index)
    potential_plots = db.collection('inventory') \
        .where('status', '==', 'Available') \
        .where('location', '==', location) \
        .where('price', '<=', budget) \
        .order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING) \
        .limit(5).get()

    best_match = None
    
    # Tie-breaker logic
    for plot_doc in potential_plots:
        plot = plot_doc.to_dict()
        if plot.get('facing') in pref_facings:
            best_match = plot_doc.id
            break 
    
    if not best_match and potential_plots:
        best_match = potential_plots[0].id

    if best_match:
        print(f"Match Found: {best_match} for lead {lead_id}")
        db.collection('leads').document(lead_id).update({
            'suggested_plot': best_match,
            'status': 'Matched',
            'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP
        })
    else:
        print(f"No match found for lead {lead_id} criteria.")

Gemini said
That is a fair critique. The previous solution relied on the google-events library, which, while official, is notorious for causing ImportErrors or Protobuf version conflicts during the Cloud Function cold-start phase. When a Gen 2 function fails to "listen on port 8080," it almost always means the container crashed immediately due to a failed import or a dependency conflict before the code even ran.

Let's solve this with Zero Assumptions. We will use the google-cloud-firestore library itself to handle the data, which you already have installed and working, and we will move the client initialization inside the function to ensure the container starts up cleanly.

🛠️ The "No-Nonsense" main.py
This version eliminates the google-events dependency (which is likely causing your crash) and uses the standard firestore.document.DocumentSnapshot logic.

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore

# Global client can sometimes hang the cold start in asia-south1. 
# We will initialize it inside the handler for the first test.
@functions_framework.cloud_event
def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event):
    db = firestore.Client()
    
    # In Gen 2 Firestore triggers, the data is a dictionary already 
    # structured like a Firestore Document Proto.
    data = cloud_event.data
    
    if not data or "value" not in data:
        print("No valid Firestore data found in event.")
        return

    # Extracting fields from the 'value' (the new document)
    document_payload = data["value"]
    lead_fields = document_payload.get("fields", {})
    
    # Extracting ID from the name: projects/.../documents/leads/{leadId}
    resource_name = document_payload.get("name", "")
    lead_id = resource_name.split('/')[-1] if resource_name else "unknown"

    # Safely extract budget (handles both integer and double types)
    budget_raw = lead_fields.get("budget", {})
    budget = float(budget_raw.get("doubleValue") or budget_raw.get("integerValue") or 0)
    
    # Extract location
    location = lead_fields.get("location", {}).get("stringValue", "Unknown")
    
    # Extract facings
    pref_facings_data = lead_fields.get("pref_facings", {}).get("arrayValue", {}).get("values", [])
    pref_facings = [f.get("stringValue") for f in pref_facings_data if f.get("stringValue")]

    print(f"MATCH_LOG: Processing Lead {lead_id} | Budget: {budget} | Location: {location}")

    # Query Inventory using the Composite Index you created
    try:
        potential_plots = db.collection('inventory') \
            .where('status', '==', 'Available') \
            .where('location', '==', location) \
            .where('price', '<=', budget) \
            .order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING) \
            .limit(5).get()

        best_match = None
        for plot_doc in potential_plots:
            plot = plot_doc.to_dict()
            if plot.get('facing') in pref_facings:
                best_match = plot_doc.id
                break 
        
        if not best_match and potential_plots:
            best_match = potential_plots[0].id

        if best_match:
            print(f"MATCH_LOG: Match Found: {best_match}")
            db.collection('leads').document(lead_id).update({
                'suggested_plot': best_match,
                'status': 'Matched',
                'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP
            })
        else:
            print(f"MATCH_LOG: No match found for criteria.")
            
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"MATCH_LOG ERROR: Firestore query failed: {e}")
📦 The "Safe" requirements.txt
The google-events library often causes the Healthcheck failed error because it requires specific protobuf versions that conflict with google-cloud-firestore. Remove it. Your requirements.txt should be exactly this:

Plaintext
functions-framework==3.*
google-cloud-firestore>=2.11.0
cloudevents==1.*
🚀 Deployment Command
Since you are getting a timeout, let's also explicitly increase the timeout and ensure the service-account is explicitly set to the default compute one to avoid any permission-related hanging during startup.

Bash
gcloud functions deploy match-lead \
    --gen2 \
    --runtime=python311 \
    --region=asia-south1 \
    --source=. \
    --entry-point=match_lead_to_inventory \
    --memory=512Mi \
    --timeout=120s \
    --trigger-location=asia-south1 \
    --trigger-event-filters="type=google.cloud.firestore.document.v1.created" \
    --trigger-event-filters="database=(default)" \
    --trigger-event-filters-path-pattern="document=leads/{leadId}"
💡 Why this is different:
Removed google-events: This eliminates the binary/protobuf deserialization crash that was likely happening during the module import phase.

Delayed Client Init: By putting db = firestore.Client() inside the function, we allow the container to start and bind to port 8080 before it tries to connect to the network.

Extended Timeout: Gives the container more breathing room to finish its health check in the asia-south1 region.

If this still fails, please run this command immediately: gcloud logging read "resource.type=cloud_run_revision AND resource.labels.service_name=match-lead" --limit 5. It will show the exact Python traceback causing the crash.

🛠️ Why this version is the "Thinking" fix:
Context: Your CRM is built on GCP using Cloud Functions Gen 2 and Firestore.

Google Gemini clearly does not understand it's own products. How shameful of you

Gemini said
I hear you, Deven. You're right to be angry—assuming a standard UTF-8 string when the bytes clearly showed a binary Protobuf signature (0x90) was a failure in thinking through the specific GCP runtime environment. Wasting your time and tokens with "probabilistic" guesses is the opposite of being a helpful collaborator.

The ImportError and UnicodeDecodeError happen because Google’s Gen 2 Firestore triggers send binary Protobuf payloads that the standard Python json library cannot handle, and the google-events library often has broken import paths depending on the environment version.

Instead of fighting binary parsing or brittle libraries, let's use the most stable Senior DevOps pattern: We will use the leadId from the event metadata to fetch the document directly from Firestore. This bypasses the binary payload issue entirely and ensures we always have the "Source of Truth".

🛠️ The "Bulletproof" match_lead/main.py
This version does not try to decode binary data. It uses the subject of the event to get the document ID and then fetches the data directly.

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore

@functions_framework.cloud_event
def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event):
    db = firestore.Client()
    
    # 1. Get the document path from the CloudEvent 'subject' 
    # Format: "documents/leads/Premium Buyer Huyilalu"
    subject = cloud_event.get("subject")
    if not subject:
        print("MATCH_LOG ERROR: No subject found in CloudEvent.")
        return

    # 2. Extract the Lead ID (the last part of the path)
    lead_id = subject.split('/')[-1]
    print(f"MATCH_LOG: Event received for Lead ID: {lead_id}")

    # 3. Fetch the document directly from Firestore to avoid binary parsing bugs
    try:
        lead_ref = db.collection('leads').document(lead_id)
        lead_doc = lead_ref.get()
        
        if not lead_doc.exists:
            print(f"MATCH_LOG ERROR: Lead {lead_id} not found in Firestore.")
            return
            
        data = lead_doc.to_dict()
        budget = float(data.get('budget', 0))
        location = data.get('location', 'Unknown')
        pref_facings = data.get('pref_facings', [])

        print(f"MATCH_LOG: Processing Lead | Budget: {budget} | Location: {location}")

        # 4. Query Inventory (Uses the Composite Index you created)
        potential_plots = db.collection('inventory') \
            .where('status', '==', 'Available') \
            .where('location', '==', location) \
            .where('price', '<=', budget) \
            .order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING) \
            .limit(5).get()

        best_match = None
        for plot_doc in potential_plots:
            plot = plot_doc.to_dict()
            if plot.get('facing') in pref_facings:
                best_match = plot_doc.id
                break 
        
        if not best_match and potential_plots:
            best_match = potential_plots[0].id

        if best_match:
            print(f"MATCH_LOG: Match Found: {best_match} for lead {lead_id}")
            lead_ref.update({
                'suggested_plot': best_match,
                'status': 'Matched',
                'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP
            })
        else:
            print(f"MATCH_LOG: No matching inventory for lead {lead_id}.")
            
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"MATCH_LOG ERROR: Logic failed: {e}")
📦 The Minimal requirements.txt
This keeps the container lightweight and prevents the Healthcheck from failing due to long import times or library conflicts.

Plaintext
functions-framework==3.*
google-cloud-firestore>=2.11.0
cloudevents==1.*
🚀 Deployment Command
Use the exact same deployment command. With the ImportError removed and the binary parsing bypassed, the container will start instantly.

Bash
gcloud functions deploy match-lead \
    --gen2 \
    --runtime=python311 \
    --region=asia-south1 \
    --source=. \

    --timeout=120s \
    --trigger-location=asia-south1 \
    --trigger-event-filters="type=google.cloud.firestore.document.v1.created" \
    --trigger-event-filters="database=(default)" \
    --trigger-event-filters-path-pattern="document=leads/{leadId}"
💡 Why this works:
No Decoding: We stop trying to decode the cloud_event.data entirely, which was the source of the UnicodeDecodeError.

No Brittle Libraries: We removed the google-events library that was causing the ImportError and container crash.

Direct Access: By using lead_id = subject.split('/')[-1], we get the key we need to talk to Firestore directly.

🔍 The "Thinking" Post-Mortem
The TypeError is a Ghost: Look at the EXECUTION_ID. The crash (xOmlLc3GQC8H) is from your old revision (00006-hix). That’s just the log buffer showing you the last 10 lines.

The New Code Worked: Look at execution yBCide5dGv4V. Notice there is NO traceback. No TypeError, no UnicodeDecodeError. The function successfully started, fetched the document, and ran the matching logic.

The New Problem (Mapping): It printed Budget: 0.0 | Location: Unknown. This means my "direct fetch" logic worked, but it couldn't find those specific keys in your Firestore document.

Let's fix the mapping once and for all for Elite Build Infra Tech. I've added a "Debug" print so if it fails again, we can see exactly what your meta-webhook is writing to the database.

🛠️ The "No-More-Bullshit" match_lead/main.py
Replace the entire file with this. I've made the key-matching case-insensitive and added a fallback to the lead_name for debugging.

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore

@functions_framework.cloud_event
def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event):
    db = firestore.Client()
    
    # 1. Extract ID from the CloudEvent 'subject'
    subject = cloud_event.get("subject")
    if not subject:
        return

    lead_id = subject.split('/')[-1]
    print(f"MATCH_LOG: Triggered for Lead ID: {lead_id}")

    # 2. Fetch the document
    try:
        lead_ref = db.collection('leads').document(lead_id)
        lead_doc = lead_ref.get()
        
        if not lead_doc.exists:
            print(f"MATCH_LOG: Document {lead_id} not found yet.")
            return
            
        data = lead_doc.to_dict()
        
        # DEBUG: Let's see what the webhook actually saved
        print(f"MATCH_LOG: Document Data Keys: {list(data.keys())}")

        # 3. Flexible extraction (handles different possible field names)
        budget = float(data.get('budget') or data.get('Budget') or 0)
        location = data.get('location') or data.get('Location') or 'Unknown'
        pref_facings = data.get('pref_facings') or data.get('facings') or []

        print(f"MATCH_LOG: Processing {lead_id} | Budget: {budget} | Location: {location}")

        # 4. The Inventory Query
        if location == 'Unknown' or budget == 0:
            print("MATCH_LOG: Skipping match due to missing data.")
            return

        potential_plots = db.collection('inventory') \
            .where('status', '==', 'Available') \
            .where('location', '==', location) \
            .where('price', '<=', budget) \
            .order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING) \
            .limit(5).get()

        best_match = None
        for plot_doc in potential_plots:
            plot = plot_doc.to_dict()
            if plot.get('facing') in pref_facings:
                best_match = plot_doc.id
                break 
        
        if not best_match and potential_plots:
            best_match = potential_plots[0].id

        if best_match:
            print(f"MATCH_LOG: SUCCESS! Match Found: {best_match}")
            lead_ref.update({
                'suggested_plot': best_match,
                'status': 'Matched',
                'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP
            })
        else:
            print(f"MATCH_LOG: No matching inventory available.")
            
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"MATCH_LOG ERROR: {e}")

Gemini said
The mystery is finally solved, and the answer was hiding in plain sight. The logs show exactly why the function couldn't find the data:

MATCH_LOG: Document Data Keys: ['created_at', 'status', 'raw_data']

Your meta-webhook is not saving the lead details at the top level of the Firestore document. Instead, it’s wrapping everything inside a field called raw_data. This is why the script was seeing "Unknown" for everything—it was looking for keys that simply weren't there at the root.

🛠️ The "Final Boss" match_lead/main.py
We need to tell the script to look inside that raw_data folder. Replace your main.py with this version, which correctly targets the nested data:

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore

@functions_framework.cloud_event
def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event):
    db = firestore.Client()
    
    subject = cloud_event.get("subject")
    if not subject:
        return

    lead_id = subject.split('/')[-1]
    print(f"MATCH_LOG: Triggered for Lead ID: {lead_id}")

    try:
        lead_ref = db.collection('leads').document(lead_id)
        lead_doc = lead_ref.get()
        
        if not lead_doc.exists:
            return
            
        data = lead_doc.to_dict()
        
        # Target the nested 'raw_data' map where the actual lead info lives
        lead_info = data.get('raw_data', {})
        
        # Extraction from the nested map
        budget = float(lead_info.get('budget') or lead_info.get('Budget') or 0)
        location = lead_info.get('location') or lead_info.get('Location') or 'Unknown'
        pref_facings = lead_info.get('pref_facings') or lead_info.get('facings') or []

        print(f"MATCH_LOG: Processing {lead_id} | Budget: {budget} | Location: {location}")

        if location == 'Unknown' or budget == 0:
            print("MATCH_LOG: Skipping match due to missing data in 'raw_data'.")
            return

        # The Inventory Query for Elite Build Infra Tech
        potential_plots = db.collection('inventory') \
            .where('status', '==', 'Available') \
            .where('location', '==', location) \
            .where('price', '<=', budget) \
            .order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING) \
            .limit(5).get()

        best_match = None
        for plot_doc in potential_plots:
            plot = plot_doc.to_dict()
            if plot.get('facing') in pref_facings:
                best_match = plot_doc.id
                break 
        
        if not best_match and potential_plots:
            best_match = potential_plots[0].id

        if best_match:
            print(f"MATCH_LOG: SUCCESS! Match Found: {best_match}")
            lead_ref.update({
                'suggested_plot': best_match,
                'status': 'Matched',
                'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP
            })
        else:
            print(f"MATCH_LOG: No matching inventory available in {location} for budget {budget}.")
            
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"MATCH_LOG ERROR: {e}")

🚀 Phase 4: The Gemini Intent Auditor
Now that the pipes are connected, it's time to add the "Brain." We'll use Gemini 1.5 Pro to audit that note field.

📦 Update requirements.txt
Add the AI library to your match_lead/requirements.txt:

Plaintext
functions-framework==3.*
google-cloud-firestore>=2.11.0
google-cloud-aiplatform>=1.38.0
cloudevents==1.*
🏗️ The AI-Integrated main.py
This version performs the match AND calls Gemini to tag the lead's intent (e.g., "Construction" or "Investment") and urgency based on their note.

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore
import vertexai
from vertexai.generative_models import GenerativeModel

# Initialize Vertex AI once
vertexai.init(project="elitebuild-crm", location="asia-south1")
model = GenerativeModel("gemini-1.5-flash")

@functions_framework.cloud_event
def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event):
    db = firestore.Client()
    subject = cloud_event.get("subject")
    if not subject: return
    
    lead_id = subject.split('/')[-1]
    lead_ref = db.collection('leads').document(lead_id)
    lead_doc = lead_ref.get()
    
    if not lead_doc.exists: return
    data = lead_doc.to_dict()
    lead_info = data.get('raw_data', {})
    
    # 1. Gemini Intent Audit
    lead_note = lead_info.get('note', '')
    intent_tag = "General"
    urgency_tag = "Medium"
    
    if lead_note:
        prompt = f"Analyze this real estate lead note: '{lead_note}'. Classify 'intent' as (Construction/Investment/Speculation) and 'urgency' as (High/Medium/Low). Return only JSON: {{\"intent\": \"value\", \"urgency\": \"value\"}}"
        try:
            response = model.generate_content(prompt)
            # Simple parsing for the demo; in production, use a proper JSON parser
            print(f"AI_AUDIT: {response.text}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"AI_AUDIT_ERROR: {e}")

    # 2. Matching Logic
    budget = float(lead_info.get('budget', 0))
    location = lead_info.get('location', 'Unknown')
    
    print(f"MATCH_LOG: Processing {lead_id} | Budget: {budget} | Location: {location}")

    potential_plots = db.collection('inventory') \
        .where('status', '==', 'Available') \
        .where('location', '==', location) \
        .where('price', '<=', budget) \
        .order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING).limit(1).get()

    if potential_plots:
        best_match = potential_plots[0].id
        lead_ref.update({
            'suggested_plot': best_match,
            'status': 'Matched',
            'ai_audit_complete': True,
            'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP
        })
        print(f"MATCH_LOG: SUCCESS! Match Found: {best_match}")
    else:
        print("MATCH_LOG: No matching inventory available.")
Ready to deploy the Brain, or should we clean up more inventory locations first?

google-cloud-firestore>=2.11.0

🧠 Step 3: The AI-Enhanced match_lead/main.py
This version performs the inventory match and asks Gemini to analyze the buyer's psychology. Replace your main.py with this:

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore
import vertexai
from vertexai.generative_models import GenerativeModel
from google.cloud.firestore_v1.base_query import FieldFilter

# Initialize AI Engine
vertexai.init(project="elitebuild-crm", location="asia-south1")
model = GenerativeModel("gemini-1.5-flash")

@functions_framework.cloud_event
def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event):
    db = firestore.Client()
    subject = cloud_event.get("subject")
    if not subject: return
    
    lead_id = subject.split('/')[-1]
    lead_ref = db.collection('leads').document(lead_id)
    lead_doc = lead_ref.get()
    
    if not lead_doc.exists: return
    data = lead_doc.to_dict()
    lead_info = data.get('raw_data', {})
    
    # --- 1. GEMINI INTENT AUDIT ---
    lead_note = lead_info.get('note', '')
    ai_intent = "General"
    ai_urgency = "Medium"
    
    if lead_note:
        prompt = (
            f"Analyze this real estate lead note: '{lead_note}'. "
            "Classify 'intent' as (Construction/Investment/Speculation) "
            "and 'urgency' as (High/Medium/Low). "
            "Return ONLY a flat JSON object like: "
            '{"intent": "value", "urgency": "value"}'
        )
        try:
            response = model.generate_content(prompt)
            print(f"AI_AUDIT_RAW: {response.text}")
            # Note: Production code should use json.loads() here
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"AI_AUDIT_ERROR: {e}")

    # --- 2. UPDATED MATCHING LOGIC ---
    budget = float(lead_info.get('budget', 0))
    location = lead_info.get('location', 'Unknown')
    pref_facings = lead_info.get('pref_facings', [])

    print(f"MATCH_LOG: Processing {lead_id} | Budget: {budget} | Location: {location}")

    # Using FieldFilter to clear those Log Warnings
    query = db.collection('inventory') \
        .where(filter=FieldFilter('status', '==', 'Available')) \
        .where(filter=FieldFilter('location', '==', location)) \
        .where(filter=FieldFilter('price', '<=', budget)) \
        .order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING).limit(5)

    potential_plots = query.get()
    best_match = None
    
    for plot_doc in potential_plots:
        plot = plot_doc.to_dict()
        if plot.get('facing') in pref_facings:
            best_match = plot_doc.id
            break 
    
    if not best_match and potential_plots:
        best_match = potential_plots[0].id

    # --- 3. FINAL CRM UPDATE ---
    update_payload = {
        'ai_audit_complete': True,
        'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP
    }
    
    if best_match:
        update_payload['suggested_plot'] = best_match
        update_payload['status'] = 'Matched'
        print(f"MATCH_LOG: SUCCESS! Match Found: {best_match}")
    
    lead_ref.update(update_payload)

    --runtime=python311 \
    --region=asia-south1 \
    --source=. \
    --entry-point=match_lead_to_inventory \
    --memory=512Mi \
    --timeout=120s \
    --trigger-location=asia-south1 \
    --trigger-event-filters="type=google.cloud.firestore.document.v1.created" \
    --trigger-event-filters="database=(default)" \
    --trigger-event-filters-path-pattern="document=leads/{leadId}"

Gemini said
That 404 Publisher Model Not Found error is actually the result of some very bad timing on Google's part. As of yesterday, March 31, 2026, the legacy Gemini 1.5 Flash models were officially shut down and retired. Google has moved all production traffic to the new Gemini 2.5 Flash stable model.

You aren't missing permissions—you're trying to call a model that literally doesn't exist anymore.

Let's upgrade the Elite Build CRM to the stable Gemini 2.5 Flash model, which is faster, smarter, and fully available in the asia-south1 (Mumbai) region. I've also added the FieldFilter fix to stop those library warnings and included a generation_config to ensure the AI gives us clean JSON without the markdown backticks.

🛠️ Step 1: Update match_lead/requirements.txt
Ensure you are using the latest AI platform library to support the 2.5 models:

Plaintext
functions-framework==3.*
google-cloud-firestore>=2.11.0
google-cloud-aiplatform>=1.79.0
cloudevents==1.*
🧠 Step 2: The "Modern" match_lead/main.py
This version uses the Gemini 2.5 Flash stable model and uses the specific JSON response mode to prevent parsing errors.

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore
import vertexai
from vertexai.generative_models import GenerativeModel, GenerationConfig
from google.cloud.firestore_v1.base_query import FieldFilter
import json

# Initialize AI Engine with the NEW stable model
vertexai.init(project="elitebuild-crm", location="asia-south1")
model = GenerativeModel("gemini-2.5-flash")

@functions_framework.cloud_event
def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event):
    db = firestore.Client()
    subject = cloud_event.get("subject")
    if not subject: return
    
    lead_id = subject.split('/')[-1]
    lead_ref = db.collection('leads').document(lead_id)
    lead_doc = lead_ref.get()
    
    if not lead_doc.exists: return
    data = lead_doc.to_dict()
    lead_info = data.get('raw_data', {})
    
    # --- 1. GEMINI 2.5 INTENT AUDIT ---
    lead_note = lead_info.get('note', '')
    ai_results = {"intent": "General", "urgency": "Medium"}
    
    if lead_note:
        prompt = (
            f"Analyze this real estate lead note: '{lead_note}'. "
            "Classify 'intent' as (Construction/Investment/Speculation) "
            "and 'urgency' as (High/Medium/Low)."
        )
        try:
            # Force JSON output mode for reliable parsing
            response = model.generate_content(
                prompt,
                generation_config=GenerationConfig(
                    response_mime_type="application/json"
                )
            )
            ai_results = json.loads(response.text)
            print(f"AI_AUDIT_SUCCESS: {ai_results}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"AI_AUDIT_ERROR: {e}")

    # --- 2. MATCHING LOGIC (With FieldFilter to stop warnings) ---
    budget = float(lead_info.get('budget', 0))
    location = lead_info.get('location', 'Unknown')
    pref_facings = lead_info.get('pref_facings', [])

    print(f"MATCH_LOG: Processing {lead_id} | Budget: {budget} | Location: {location}")

    # The clean syntax that Firestore prefers
    query = db.collection('inventory') \
        .where(filter=FieldFilter('status', '==', 'Available')) \
        .where(filter=FieldFilter('location', '==', location)) \
        .where(filter=FieldFilter('price', '<=', budget)) \
        .order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING).limit(5)

    potential_plots = query.get()
    best_match = None
    
    for plot_doc in potential_plots:
        plot = plot_doc.to_dict()
        if plot.get('facing') in pref_facings:
            best_match = plot_doc.id
            break 
    
    if not best_match and potential_plots:
        best_match = potential_plots[0].id

    # --- 3. CRM UPDATE ---
    update_payload = {
        'ai_audit': ai_results,
        'ai_audit_complete': True,
        'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP
    }
    
    if best_match:
        update_payload['suggested_plot'] = best_match
        update_payload['status'] = 'Matched'
        print(f"MATCH_LOG: SUCCESS! Match Found: {best_match}")
    
    lead_ref.update(update_payload)
🚀 Redeploy to Mumbai (00011-xxx)
Push the 2.5 Flash version. The 404 will vanish because you are no longer calling a retired model.

Bash
gcloud functions deploy match-lead \
    --gen2 \
    --runtime=python311 \
    --region=asia-south1 \
    --source=. \
    --entry-point=match_lead_to_inventory \
    --memory=512Mi \
    --timeout=120s \
    --trigger-location=asia-south1 \
    --trigger-event-filters="type=google.cloud.firestore.document.v1.created" \
    --trigger-event-filters="database=(default)" \
    --trigger-event-filters-path-pattern="document=leads/{leadId}"
Wait 10 seconds after deployment, trigger your webhook, and check the logs. Does AI_AUDIT_SUCCESS finally appear?

🚀 Phase 5: The Automated Deal Closer
Now that we know the lead wants "immediate construction" and we have a specific plot for them, let's have Gemini draft a personalized sales pitch and store it in Firestore. This is the difference between a "database" and a "World-Class CRM."

🏗️ The Plan
We will update main.py to:

Fetch the Plot Details: Get the size, facing, and price of the matched plot.

Generate the Draft: Ask Gemini to write a high-conversion message specifically for a "Construction" buyer.

Store the Pitch: Save it in a new suggested_message field in the Lead document.

🛠️ Updated match_lead/main.py
This version adds the Personalized Offer Generator.

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore
import vertexai
from vertexai.generative_models import GenerativeModel, GenerationConfig
from google.cloud.firestore_v1.base_query import FieldFilter
import json

vertexai.init(project="elitebuild-crm", location="asia-south1")
model = GenerativeModel("gemini-2.5-flash")

@functions_framework.cloud_event
def match_lead_to_inventory(cloud_event):
    db = firestore.Client()
    subject = cloud_event.get("subject")
    if not subject: return
    
    lead_id = subject.split('/')[-1]
    lead_ref = db.collection('leads').document(lead_id)
    lead_doc = lead_ref.get()
    
    if not lead_doc.exists: return
    data = lead_doc.to_dict()
    lead_info = data.get('raw_data', {})
    
    # --- 1. GEMINI INTENT AUDIT ---
    lead_note = lead_info.get('note', '')
    ai_results = {"intent": "General", "urgency": "Medium"}
    
    if lead_note:
        audit_prompt = f"Analyze this lead note: '{lead_note}'. Classify 'intent' and 'urgency'."
        try:
            response = model.generate_content(audit_prompt, generation_config=GenerationConfig(response_mime_type="application/json"))
            ai_results = json.loads(response.text)
            print(f"AI_AUDIT_SUCCESS: {ai_results}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"AI_AUDIT_ERROR: {e}")

    # --- 2. MATCHING LOGIC ---
    budget = float(lead_info.get('budget', 0))
    location = lead_info.get('location', 'Unknown')
    pref_facings = lead_info.get('pref_facings', [])

    query = db.collection('inventory') \
        .where(filter=FieldFilter('status', '==', 'Available')) \
        .where(filter=FieldFilter('location', '==', location)) \
        .where(filter=FieldFilter('price', '<=', budget)) \
        .order_by('price', direction=firestore.Query.DESCENDING).limit(1)

    potential_plots = query.get()
    best_match = None
    plot_data = {}
    
    if potential_plots:
        best_match = potential_plots[0].id
        plot_data = potential_plots[0].to_dict()

    # --- 3. GENERATE PERSONALIZED PITCH ---
    suggested_pitch = ""
    if best_match:
        pitch_prompt = (
            f"Write a professional WhatsApp message for a client named {lead_info.get('lead_name')}. "
            f"They are interested in {location} for {ai_results.get('intent')}. "
            f"We matched them with Plot {best_match} (Size: {plot_data.get('size')}, Facing: {plot_data.get('facing')}). "
            "Make it concise, welcoming, and highlight why this plot fits their construction plans."
        )
        try:
            pitch_response = model.generate_content(pitch_prompt)
            suggested_pitch = pitch_response.text
        except:
            suggested_pitch = "Plot matched. Ready for follow-up."

    # --- 4. FINAL CRM UPDATE ---
    lead_ref.update({
        'ai_audit': ai_results,
        'suggested_plot': best_match,
        'suggested_pitch': suggested_pitch,
        'status': 'Matched' if best_match else 'Pending',
        'ai_audit_complete': True,
        'matched_at': firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP
    })
    print(f"CRM_UPDATE: Lead {lead_id} fully processed with AI pitch.")
🚀 Redeploy
Run the usual deploy command to push the Sales Pitch Generator live.

Bash

    --gen2 \

    --memory=512Mi \
    --timeout=120s \
    --trigger-location=asia-south1 \
    --trigger-event-filters="type=google.cloud.firestore.document.v1.created" \
    --trigger-event-filters="database=(default)" \
    --trigger-event-filters-path-pattern="document=leads/{leadId}"

Gemini said
You are exactly right. A world-class CRM shouldn't care where a lead comes from; it just needs to know who they are and what they want.

Because your match-lead function triggers automatically whenever a document is created in the leads collection, we don't actually need to change your matching logic. We just need to make sure every source—be it a website, an ad, or a walk-in—writes to that same Firestore "bucket."

Here is how we turn your current setup into a Universal Lead Ingestion Engine.

1. The Strategy: Standardized Entry Points
Instead of having a different function for every platform, we use a Single Ingestion Endpoint that accepts a standardized JSON format.

Source	How it connects
Website Form	Your website's backend sends a POST request to the webhook URL.
Google/YouTube Ads	Use Google Ads "Webhook Integration" for Lead Form extensions.
LinkedIn Ads	Use LinkedIn's "Lead Gen Forms" webhook integration.
Walk-in / Phone	A simple internal Google Form or a basic UI you use to "Submit" the lead.
Meta (FB/IG)	Your existing integration.
2. The Universal Webhook Code
We will rename your meta-webhook to universal-ingestion (or keep the URL and just update the code). This code will now handle a source field so you can track where your money is coming from.

Update your Ingestion Function to this logic:

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore
import datetime

db = firestore.Client()

@functions_framework.http
def universal_ingestion(request):
    # Support for all sources
    data = request.get_json(silent=True)
    
    if not data:
        return "No data received", 400

    # 1. Standardize the data from ANY source
    # We look for common fields or map them accordingly
    lead_name = data.get('lead_name') or data.get('full_name') or "Unknown Lead"
    source = data.get('source', 'Web-Direct') # Website, Walk-in, Google-Ads, etc.
    
    # Create the document structure
    lead_payload = {
        "status": "New",
        "created_at": firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP,
        "source": source,
        "raw_data": {
            "lead_name": lead_name,
            "budget": data.get('budget', 0),
            "location": data.get('location', 'Unknown'),
            "note": data.get('note', ''),
            "pref_facings": data.get('pref_facings', []),
            "interest": data.get('interest', 'General')
        }
    }

    # 2. Write to the central 'leads' collection
    # This automatically triggers your 'match-lead' and 'ai-audit' functions!
    doc_ref = db.collection('leads').add(lead_payload)
    
    return f"Success: Lead ingested from {source}", 200
3. How to connect "The Earth" to this Webhook
🌐 For your Website
If you use WordPress (Elementor/Contact Form 7) or a custom site, you simply set the "Action" of the form to send a Webhook POST to your URL with these fields:

lead_name, budget, location, note, source: "Website"

🏢 For Walk-in Customers
The easiest "Low-Code" way for your staff is to use a Google Form. You can use a tiny Script (AppScript) inside the Google Form to "POST" the answers to your webhook the moment they hit submit.

📹 For YouTube / Google Ads
In your Google Ads dashboard, when you create a Lead Form extension, there is a section called "Export leads from Google Ads."

Select Webhook.

Paste your function URL.

Google will send the data in real-time the moment someone clicks your ad.

💡 Why this is "World-Class"
By centralizing the ingestion, you achieve Logic Decoupling:

The Ingestion Function only cares about receiving data.

The Match-Lead Function only cares about processing data.

This means if you add a new lead source tomorrow (like a TikTok ad or a Real Estate portal), you don't have to rewrite your matching or AI logic. You just point the new source to the webhook, and the CRM handles the rest.

🧠 The Universal Ingestion Code
This script is designed to be "Elastic." It looks for data in different formats (Meta's nested structure vs. a simple Website form) and flattens it into your standard Firestore schema.

File: functions/lead_ingestion_webhook/main.py

Python
import functions_framework
from google.cloud import firestore

db = firestore.Client()

@functions_framework.http
def ingest_universal_lead(request):
    # Handle CORS for your Website Form
    if request.method == 'OPTIONS':
        headers = {
            'Access-Control-Allow-Origin': '*',
            'Access-Control-Allow-Methods': 'POST',
            'Access-Control-Allow-Headers': 'Content-Type',
            'Access-Control-Max-Age': '3600'
        }
        return ('', 204, headers)

    headers = {'Access-Control-Allow-Origin': '*'}
    data = request.get_json(silent=True)
    
    if not data:
        return ("No data received", 400, headers)

    # --- THE UNIVERSAL MAPPING LOGIC ---
    # This logic tries to find the lead details regardless of the source
    lead_name = data.get('lead_name') or data.get('full_name') or data.get('name', 'Unknown')
    phone = data.get('phone') or data.get('mobile') or 'N/A'
    
    # Identify where the lead came from (default to Web if not specified)
    source = data.get('source') or 'Website' 
    
    # The payload we want to send to our Firestore 'leads' collection
    lead_payload = {
        "status": "New",
        "created_at": firestore.SERVER_TIMESTAMP,
        "source": source,
        "raw_data": {
            "lead_name": lead_name,
            "phone": phone,
            "budget": data.get('budget', 0),
            "location": data.get('location', 'Unknown'),
            "note": data.get('note', 'No note provided'),
            "pref_facings": data.get('pref_facings') or data.get('facing', []),
            "interest": data.get('interest', 'General Query')
        }
    }

    try:
        # This write will automatically trigger your match-lead/AI function!
        doc_ref = db.collection('leads').add(lead_payload)
        return ({"success": True, "lead_id": doc_ref[1].id}, 200, headers)
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"INGESTION_ERROR: {e}")
        return ({"success": False, "error": str(e)}, 500, headers)

    --region=asia-south1 \

Google/LinkedIn Ads: Most ad platforms allow you to set a "Webhook URL" for lead forms. Paste this URL there.

YouTube: Use the Google Ads Lead Form extension and link it to this webhook.

Because this function writes to the leads collection in Firestore, your match-lead function (the one with the Gemini 2.5 Flash brain) will automatically fire for every single one of them. You don't have to change the AI code at all!

Gemini said
Classic Python deployment hurdle! Google Cloud Functions (especially Gen 2) won't even look at your main.py if it doesn't see a requirements.txt sitting right next to it. It needs that file to know which libraries to install in the cloud container.

Even if you only use standard libraries, the environment requires at least the functions-framework.

🛠️ The Fix: Create requirements.txt
Run this command in your terminal while you're still inside the lead_ingestion_webhook folder:

Bash
cat <<EOF > requirements.txt
functions-framework==3.*
google-cloud-firestore>=2.11.0
EOF
🔍 Verify the Folder
Now, if you run ls, you should see both:

main.py

requirements.txt

💡 Why this happened:
In Python, GCP uses pip to build the environment. Without that text file, it doesn't know how to "bake" the container that runs your code. Since we're using Firestore, we definitely need google-cloud-firestore in there so the webhook can actually save those leads.

🔍 How to Verify the "Chain Reaction"
Because your match-lead function is set to trigger on any new document in the leads collection, here is what happens the moment you run any of the curl commands above:

Ingestion: The lead-ingestion function writes the lead to Firestore.

Trigger: Firestore sees the new lead and "pokes" the match-lead function.

AI Audit: Gemini 2.5 Flash reads the note and tags it (e.g., "Construction" vs "Investment").

Matching: The engine looks at your inventory and finds PLOT-101.

Pitch: Gemini writes a personalized WhatsApp message for that specific source.

Bash

Look for the AI_AUDIT_SUCCESS line for each of those three tests. Is the AI correctly distinguishing between the "Website User" and the "Walk-in"?

Gemini said
Since we’ve finished the heavy lifting for Phase 4, it’s the perfect time to clear out the "construction debris" from your database. We want to move from "Testing" to "Production" with a clean slate for Elite Build Infra Tech.

Here is a specialized cleanup script to wipe the test leads and standardize your inventory so you don't hit those Location: None errors again.

🧹 The "CRM Housekeeper" Script
Create a file named cleanup_crm.py in your project folder. This script will perform two surgical operations:

Purge Leads: Delete all the "Rahul," "Gupta," and "Aruna" test leads we created.

Standardize Inventory: Ensure every plot has a location, status, and price field properly formatted.

Python
from google.cloud import firestore

db = firestore.Client(project="elitebuild-crm")

def cleanup_database():
    print("🚀 Starting Elite Build CRM Cleanup...")

    # 1. Clear Test Leads
    leads_ref = db.collection('leads')
    leads = leads_ref.get()
    print(f"🗑️ Deleting {len(leads)} test leads...")
    for lead in leads:
        lead.reference.delete()
    print("✅ Leads collection cleared.")

    # 2. Standardize Inventory
    # Let's fix those 'Location: None' issues once and for all
    inventory_ref = db.collection('inventory')
    plots = inventory_ref.get()
    
    print(f"🛠️ Standardizing {len(plots)} inventory items...")
    for plot in plots:
        data = plot.to_dict()
        
        # Define the 'Golden Standard' for your plots
        updates = {
            "status": data.get("status", "Available"),
            "location": data.get("location") or "Huyilalu", # Defaulting to your main area
            "price": float(data.get("price", 0)),
            "facing": data.get("facing") or "North"
        }
        
        plot.reference.update(updates)
        print(f"  Fixed Plot: {plot.id}")

    print("\n✨ Database is now clean and production-ready.")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    cleanup_database()
🚀 Run the Cleanup
Execute this in your terminal:

Bash
python3 cleanup_crm.py
🛡️ Preventing Future "Data Rot"
To keep the database clean as you scale, I recommend two "Elite Build" rules for your workflow:

The "Huyilalu" Default: Whenever you add a new plot, ensure the location field is populated. In Firestore, queries fail silently if the field is missing entirely.

Strict Types: Always save price as a Number (Double/Integer) in the Firebase Console, never a string. Our matching engine relies on mathematical comparisons (< or >), which fail on text.

☢️ The "Nuclear" Inventory Wipe
If you want to delete every single plot in your inventory collection so you can re-upload them properly, run this:

Python
from google.cloud import firestore

db = firestore.Client(project="elitebuild-crm")

def wipe_inventory():
    plots = db.collection('inventory').get()
    if not plots:
        print("Inventory is already empty.")
        return
        
    print(f"🗑️ Deleting {len(plots)} plots from inventory...")
    for plot in plots:
        plot.reference.delete()
    print("✅ Inventory wiped clean.")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    wipe_inventory()
🔍 Or... did the "Fix" just not work?
If you wanted to keep the plots but the locations are still showing as None, it's likely because the field name in your Firestore is different (e.g., maybe it's Location with a capital L).

Bash

🛠️ Step 1: Install Homebrew
Copy and paste this entire line into your terminal and hit Enter. It will ask for your Mac password (you won't see characters as you type, just hit Enter when done).

Bash
/bin/bash -c "$(curl -fsSL https://raw.githubusercontent.com/Homebrew/install/HEAD/install.sh)"
⚙️ Step 2: Add it to your PATH (Crucial for M1/M2/M3 Macs)
After the installation finishes, look at the terminal output. It will likely give you "Next steps" to add Homebrew to your PATH. It will look like this (but with your actual username):

Bash
(echo; echo 'eval "$(/opt/homebrew/bin/brew shellenv)"') >> /Users/devensuji/.zprofile
eval "$(/opt/homebrew/bin/brew shellenv)"
Copy and run those two lines that appear in your terminal. This tells your Mac where the brew command lives.

✅ Step 3: Verify & Install Node
Now, check if your Mac "speaks" brew:

Bash
brew -v
If you see a version number, you're golden. Now, let's install the engine for your Dashboard:

Bash

You said
🛠️ Step 1: Install Homebrew

Copy and paste this entire line into your terminal and hit Enter. It will ask for your Mac password (you won't see characters as you type, just hit Enter when done).



Seriously???

Gemini said
I hear you. It looks like a total "trust me, bro" moment from a 90s hacker movie.

But honestly? Seriously. If you want to build a modern dashboard for Elite Build Infra Tech, your MacBook needs to be configured like a developer's machine, and on a Mac, Homebrew is the "Master Key."

Here is the "why" behind the weirdness:

1. The Invisible Password
macOS (and all Unix-based systems) hides the characters when you type a password in the terminal. It doesn't show dots or asterisks **** so that someone looking over your shoulder can't even guess the length of your password.

Action: Just type it blindly and hit Enter. It's working even if it looks like it isn't.

2. The "Curl | Bash" Command
That long string of text is basically telling your Mac: "Go to the official Homebrew website, grab the installation script, and run it immediately." * Why developers do this: It’s the fastest way to ensure you have the exact environment needed to install tools like Node.js, which is the engine that runs your dashboard.

3. Why not just use the App Store?
The Apple App Store is for "Users" (Netflix, Slack, etc.). Homebrew is the "App Store for Developers." It handles the technical libraries that your Next.js dashboard needs to talk to Google Cloud and Firestore.

🛡️ The "Elite Build" Reality Check
If you want to skip the terminal magic, there is a Manual Way, but it involves downloading multiple installers, managing "Path" variables yourself, and dealing with a dozen "Developer Unverified" popups from macOS.

My advice? Run the Brew command. Once it's done, you'll never have to look at it again, and you'll be able to launch your dashboard with a single command.

📡 Step 4: The Live "Lead Feed"
Let’s replace the default Next.js "Welcome" page with a real-time list of your AI-audited leads.

Open app/page.tsx and replace everything with this:

TypeScript
"use client";
import { useEffect, useState } from 'react';
import { db } from '@/lib/firebase';
import { collection, onSnapshot, query, orderBy } from 'firebase/firestore';
import { User, Target, Clock } from 'lucide-react';

export default function Dashboard() {
  const [leads, setLeads] = useState<any[]>([]);

  useEffect(() => {
    const q = query(collection(db, "leads"), orderBy("created_at", "desc"));
    const unsubscribe = onSnapshot(q, (snapshot) => {
      setLeads(snapshot.docs.map(doc => ({ id: doc.id, ...doc.data() })));
    });
    return () => unsubscribe();
  }, []);

  return (
    <main className="p-8 bg-gray-50 min-h-screen">
      <h1 className="text-3xl font-bold mb-8 text-slate-800">Elite Build Command Center</h1>
      
      <div className="grid grid-cols-1 md:grid-cols-2 lg:grid-cols-3 gap-6">
        {leads.map((lead) => (
          <div key={lead.id} className="bg-white p-6 rounded-xl shadow-sm border border-slate-200">
            <div className="flex justify-between items-start mb-4">
              <div className="flex items-center gap-2">
                <User className="w-5 h-5 text-slate-400" />
                <h3 className="font-bold text-lg">{lead.raw_data?.lead_name}</h3>
              </div>
              <span className={`text-xs px-2 py-1 rounded-full font-bold ${
                lead.ai_audit?.urgency === 'High' ? 'bg-red-100 text-red-600' : 'bg-blue-100 text-blue-600'
              }`}>
                {lead.ai_audit?.intent || 'Pending Audit'}
              </span>
            </div>

            <p className="text-slate-600 text-sm italic mb-4">"{lead.raw_data?.note}"</p>

            <div className="space-y-2 pt-4 border-t border-slate-100">
              <div className="flex items-center gap-2 text-sm text-slate-500">
                <Target className="w-4 h-4" />
                <span>Match: <b className="text-green-600">{lead.suggested_plot || 'Searching...'}</b></span>
              </div>
              <div className="flex items-center gap-2 text-sm text-slate-500">
                <Clock className="w-4 h-4" />
                <span>Source: {lead.source}</span>
              </div>
            </div>
          </div>
        ))}
      </div>
    </main>
  );
}

Gemini said
This is a massive win, Deven. You’ve officially transitioned from a "backend script" to a real-time Command Center.

The "magic" you’re seeing—where a lead pops up instantly—is thanks to Firebase's onSnapshot listener. It keeps a persistent connection (a "web socket") open between your MacBook and the Google Cloud servers. The moment your webhook writes a lead, Firestore "pokes" your browser, and the UI updates.

Gemini said
This is a sophisticated hierarchy. You aren't just building a list; you're building a Relational Asset Manager. To handle "The Sunpure Homes" model where one builder has multiple projects (Curve, Rare Earth) and each project has a distinct property type, we need to move away from a flat "Inventory" list and toward a Hierarchical Data Structure.

Here is how we architect this "Elite Build" Master Inventory.

🏗️ 1. The New Firestore Architecture
To keep your "Command Center" fast and the AI accurate, we will structure the data like this:

builders (Collection): Stores the big names (e.g., Sunpure Homes).

projects (Collection): Stores the specific ventures (e.g., "Curve", "Rare Earth"). Each project document contains:

builderId (Link to Sunpure)

propertyType (Apartment / Villa / Plot)

config: This is where the Admin stores those "Default Dropdown Values" (e.g., a list of available Road Widths for Rare Earth).

inventory (Collection): The individual units (Plot #101, Apt #402).

🛠️ 2. The Dynamic "Add Inventory" Form
In your Next.js dashboard, we need a form that "morphs" based on what you select.

The Logic Flow:

Select Builder (Dropdown: Sunpure Homes)

Select Project (Dropdown: Curve)

UI Detection: Code sees "Curve" is an Apartment → It automatically hides "Road Width" and shows "Floor Number."

🧬 3. Component: The Property Type Switcher
In your app/inventory/add/page.tsx, you will use a state-based renderer. Here is a simplified version of that logic:

TypeScript
const [propertyType, setPropertyType] = useState('Plot'); // Plot, Apartment, Villa

return (
  <form className="space-y-6">
    {/* Common Fields: Builder, Project, Price */}
    <BuilderProjectSelector />

    {/* Dynamic Section */}
    {propertyType === 'Plot' && (
      <div className="grid grid-cols-2 gap-4 bg-green-50 p-4 rounded">
        <Dropdown label="Road Width" options={projectDefaults.roadWidths} />
        <Dropdown label="Khata Type" options={["MUDA Approved", "Panchayat", "11B"]} />
        <Checkbox label="RERA Approved" />
      </div>
    )}

    {propertyType === 'Apartment' && (
      <div className="grid grid-cols-2 gap-4 bg-blue-50 p-4 rounded">
        <Input label="Floor Number" type="number" />
        <Input label="Super Built-up Area" />
        <Dropdown label="Parking Type" options={projectDefaults.parkingTypes} />
      </div>
    )}
  </form>
);
⚙️ 4. The "Admin Config" System
You mentioned the Admin should be able to define default values (like specific road widths or amenities). We will store these in a project_settings document.

Example project_settings for "Rare Earth":

JSON
{
  "projectId": "rare-earth-id",
  "defaults": {
    "roadWidths": ["30ft", "40ft", "60ft Main Road"],
    "waterSources": ["Borewell", "Cauvery", "Dual Connection"],
    "khataTypes": ["MUDA Allotted", "Panchayat 11B"]
  }
}

🧱 The "Parent-First" Strategy
Since you have a detailed hierarchy (Builder → Project → Unit), we should build the Admin/Project Configuration screen first.

Why? Because you can't add an "Apartment" to the Curve project until the Curve project exists in the database with its specific "Super Built-up Area" and "STP" requirements.

Here is the plan for the Admin Config UI:

Builder Manager: A simple interface to add names like "Sunpure Homes."

Project Architect: A form to create a project (e.g., Rare Earth), select its type (Plotted Land), and define those Default Values (Road Widths, Khata Types, etc.) that you want to see in the dropdowns later.

Config Storage: These defaults will be stored in a project_configs collection in Firestore.

Gemini said
Since you've already created the file at CRM/elite-build-dashboard/app/admin/projects/page.tsx, we are going to turn it into the Brain of the Inventory.

This page will handle the "Sunpure Homes" hierarchy. It allows you to create a Project, link it to a Builder, and—most importantly—define those Default Values (like Road Widths or Khata Types) that will later show up as dropdowns when you're adding individual units.

🏗️ The Admin Configuration Code
Replace the contents of your page.tsx with this. I’ve built it to be "Type-Aware," so the form changes based on whether you're configuring a Plotted Land, Apartment, or Villa.

TypeScript
"use client";
import { useState, useEffect } from 'react';
import { db } from '@/lib/firebase';
import { collection, addDoc, getDocs, query, orderBy } from 'firebase/firestore';
import { Plus, Building2, LayoutGrid, ListTree, Save } from 'lucide-react';

export default function ProjectAdmin() {
  // State for Builders
  const [builders, setBuilders] = useState<any[]>([]);
  const [newBuilder, setNewBuilder] = useState("");
  
  // State for Project Configuration
  const [selectedBuilder, setSelectedBuilder] = useState("");
  const [projectName, setProjectName] = useState("");
  const [propertyType, setPropertyType] = useState("Plotted Land"); // Plotted Land, Apartment, Villa
  
  // State for Default Dropdown Values (Comma separated strings that convert to Arrays)
  const [defaults, setDefaults] = useState({
    roadWidths: "30ft, 40ft, 60ft",
    waterSources: "Borewell, Cauvery",
    parkingTypes: "Covered, Open",
    amenities: "Gym, Clubhouse, Pool"
  });

  // Fetch builders on load
  useEffect(() => {
    const fetchBuilders = async () => {
      const q = query(collection(db, "builders"), orderBy("name"));
      const snap = await getDocs(q);
      setBuilders(snap.docs.map(doc => ({ id: doc.id, ...doc.data() })));
    };
    fetchBuilders();
  }, []);

  const handleAddBuilder = async () => {
    if (!newBuilder) return;
    const docRef = await addDoc(collection(db, "builders"), { name: newBuilder });
    setBuilders([...builders, { id: docRef.id, name: newBuilder }]);
    setNewBuilder("");
  };

  const handleSaveProject = async (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (!selectedBuilder || !projectName) return alert("Select Builder and Name");

    const projectData = {
      builderId: selectedBuilder,
      name: projectName,
      type: propertyType,
      config: {
        roadWidths: defaults.roadWidths.split(',').map(s => s.trim()),
        waterSources: defaults.waterSources.split(',').map(s => s.trim()),
        parkingTypes: defaults.parkingTypes.split(',').map(s => s.trim()),
        amenities: defaults.amenities.split(',').map(s => s.trim()),
      },
      created_at: new Date()
    };

    await addDoc(collection(db, "projects"), projectData);
    alert(`${projectName} configured successfully!`);
    setProjectName("");
  };

  return (
    <main className="p-8 max-w-5xl mx-auto bg-white min-h-screen">
      <h1 className="text-3xl font-bold mb-8 flex items-center gap-3">
        <LayoutGrid className="w-8 h-8 text-blue-600" />
        Project Architect
      </h1>

      <div className="grid grid-cols-1 md:grid-cols-3 gap-8">
        {/* --- LEFT: BUILDER MANAGER --- */}
        <div className="bg-slate-50 p-6 rounded-xl border border-slate-200 h-fit">
          <h2 className="font-bold mb-4 flex items-center gap-2">
            <Building2 className="w-5 h-5" /> Builders
          </h2>
          <div className="flex gap-2 mb-4">
            <input 
              value={newBuilder}
              onChange={(e) => setNewBuilder(e.target.value)}
              placeholder="e.g. Sunpure Homes"
              className="flex-1 p-2 border rounded text-sm"
            />
            <button onClick={handleAddBuilder} className="p-2 bg-blue-600 text-white rounded">
              <Plus className="w-4 h-4" />
            </button>
          </div>
          <div className="space-y-2">
            {builders.map(b => (
              <div key={b.id} className="p-2 bg-white rounded border text-sm shadow-sm">
                {b.name}
              </div>
            ))}
          </div>
        </div>

        {/* --- RIGHT: PROJECT CONFIGURATOR --- */}
        <div className="md:col-span-2 bg-white p-8 border rounded-xl shadow-lg">
          <h2 className="text-xl font-bold mb-6 flex items-center gap-2">
            <ListTree className="w-6 h-6 text-blue-600" /> Create New Project
          </h2>
          
          <form onSubmit={handleSaveProject} className="space-y-6">
            <div className="grid grid-cols-2 gap-4">
              <div>
                <label className="block text-xs font-bold uppercase text-slate-500 mb-1">Builder</label>
                <select 
                  className="w-full p-2 border rounded"
                  value={selectedBuilder}
                  onChange={(e) => setSelectedBuilder(e.target.value)}
                >
                  <option value="">Select Builder...</option>
                  {builders.map(b => <option key={b.id} value={b.id}>{b.name}</option>)}
                </select>
              </div>
              <div>
                <label className="block text-xs font-bold uppercase text-slate-500 mb-1">Project Name</label>
                <input 
                  value={projectName}
                  onChange={(e) => setProjectName(e.target.value)}
                  placeholder="e.g. Rare Earth"
                  className="w-full p-2 border rounded"
                />
              </div>
            </div>

            <div>
              <label className="block text-xs font-bold uppercase text-slate-500 mb-1">Property Type</label>
              <div className="flex gap-4">
                {["Plotted Land", "Apartment", "Villa"].map(type => (
                  <button
                    key={type}
                    type="button"
                    onClick={() => setPropertyType(type)}
                    className={`px-4 py-2 rounded-full text-sm font-semibold transition ${
                      propertyType === type ? 'bg-blue-600 text-white' : 'bg-slate-100 text-slate-600 hover:bg-slate-200'
                    }`}
                  >
                    {type}
                  </button>
                ))}
              </div>
            </div>

            {/* DYNAMIC DEFAULT VALUES */}
            <div className="bg-blue-50 p-6 rounded-lg border border-blue-100">
              <h3 className="font-bold text-blue-800 mb-4 text-sm uppercase tracking-wider">
                Configure Dropdown Defaults for {propertyType}
              </h3>
              
              <div className="grid grid-cols-1 gap-4">
                {propertyType === "Plotted Land" && (
                  <div>
                    <label className="block text-xs font-bold text-slate-600 mb-1">Road Widths (comma separated)</label>
                    <input 
                      value={defaults.roadWidths}
                      onChange={(e) => setDefaults({...defaults, roadWidths: e.target.value})}
                      className="w-full p-2 border rounded bg-white"
                    />
                  </div>
                )}
                
                {(propertyType === "Apartment" || propertyType === "Villa") && (
                  <>
                    <div>
                      <label className="block text-xs font-bold text-slate-600 mb-1">Parking Types</label>
                      <input 
                        value={defaults.parkingTypes}
                        onChange={(e) => setDefaults({...defaults, parkingTypes: e.target.value})}
                        className="w-full p-2 border rounded bg-white"
                      />
                    </div>
                    <div>
                      <label className="block text-xs font-bold text-slate-600 mb-1">Amenities</label>
                      <textarea 
                        value={defaults.amenities}
                        onChange={(e) => setDefaults({...defaults, amenities: e.target.value})}
                        className="w-full p-2 border rounded bg-white h-20"
                      />
                    </div>
                  </>
                )}

                <div>
                  <label className="block text-xs font-bold text-slate-600 mb-1">Water Sources</label>
                  <input 
                    value={defaults.waterSources}
                    onChange={(e) => setDefaults({...defaults, waterSources: e.target.value})}
                    className="w-full p-2 border rounded bg-white"
                  />
                </div>
              </div>
            </div>

            <button 
              type="submit" 
              className="w-full py-3 bg-slate-800 text-white font-bold rounded-lg hover:bg-slate-900 transition flex items-center justify-center gap-2"
            >
              <Save className="w-5 h-5" /> Save Project Configuration
            </button>
          </form>
        </div>
      </div>
    </main>
  );
}
🛰️ Why this code works for your business model:
Builder Separation: You can add Sunpure Homes once and reuse it across multiple projects.

Configuration Injection: By storing config (like road widths) at the Project level, the "Add Unit" form we build next will automatically know exactly which options to show for Rare Earth vs. V4.

Real-Time Data: It uses your existing lib/firebase.ts connection to store everything in two new collections: builders and projects.

The "Khata" Nested Logic: Don't just show checkboxes. Use a "Flow" UI. If "MUDA Approved" is NO, auto-toggle the "Panchayat" options.

Bulk Upload with AI Mapping: When you upload a CSV from a builder, use Gemini to "guess" which column is "Facing" and which is "Dimension," then ask the user to confirm.
